<p><b>Nice</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Àà/: primary stress follows">Àà</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iÀê/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iÀê</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <small>French pronunciation:&#160;‚Äã</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[nis]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%A7ard" class="mw-redirect" title="Ni√ßard">Ni√ßard</a> <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>: <span lang="oc" xml:lang="oc"><i>Ni√ßa</i></span>, classical norm, or <i><span lang="oc" xml:lang="oc">Nissa</span></i>, nonstandard, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Occitan" title="Help:IPA/Occitan">[Àànisa]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>Nizza</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Italian" title="Help:IPA/Italian">[Àànittsa]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">ŒùŒØŒ∫Œ±ŒπŒ±</span>; <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Nicaea</i></span>) is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_communes_in_France_with_over_20,000_inhabitants" title="List of communes in France with over 20,000 inhabitants">fifth most populous city</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Alpes-Maritimes" title="Alpes-Maritimes">Alpes-Maritimes</a> <i>d√©partement</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Largest_urban_areas_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest urban areas of the European Union">urban area</a> of Nice extends beyond the administrative city limits, with a population of about 1 million<sup id="cite_ref-World_Urban_Areas_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Urban_Areas-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> on an area of 721&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (278&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Urban_Areas_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Urban_Areas-1">[1]</a></sup> Located in the <a href="/wiki/French_Riviera" title="French Riviera">French Riviera</a>, on the south east coast of France on the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, Nice is the second-largest French city on the Mediterranean coast and the second-largest city in the <a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-C√¥te d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-C√¥te d'Azur</a> region after <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>. Nice is about 13 kilometres (8 miles) from the principality of <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/Nice_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Nice Airport">airport</a> is a gateway to the principality as well.</p>
<p>The city is nicknamed <i>Nice la Belle</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Nissa_La_Bella" title="Nissa La Bella">Nissa La Bella</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%A7ard" class="mw-redirect" title="Ni√ßard">Ni√ßard</a>), which means <i>Nice the Beautiful</i>, which is also the title of the unofficial anthem of Nice, written by <a href="/wiki/Menica_Rondelly" title="Menica Rondelly">Menica Rondelly</a> in 1912.</p>
<p>The area of today's Nice contains <a href="/wiki/Terra_Amata_(archaeological_site)" title="Terra Amata (archaeological site)">Terra Amata</a>, an archaeological site which displays evidence of a very early use of fire. Around 350 BC, Greeks of Marseille founded a permanent settlement and called it Nikaia, after <i><a href="/wiki/Nike_(mythology)" title="Nike (mythology)">Nike</a></i>, the goddess of victory.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Through the ages, the town has changed hands many times. Its strategic location and port significantly contributed to its maritime strength. For centuries it was a dominion of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Savoy" title="Duchy of Savoy">Savoy</a>, and was then part of France between 1792 and 1815, when it was returned to <a href="/wiki/Piedmont-Sardinia" class="mw-redirect" title="Piedmont-Sardinia">Piedmont-Sardinia</a> until its re-annexation by France in 1860.</p>
<p>The natural beauty of the Nice area and its mild Mediterranean climate came to the attention of the English upper classes in the second half of the 18th century, when an increasing number of aristocratic families took to spending their winters there. The city's main seaside promenade, the <a href="/wiki/Promenade_des_Anglais" title="Promenade des Anglais">Promenade des Anglais</a> ("Walkway of the English') owes its name to visitors to the resort.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> For decades now, the picturesque Nicean surroundings have attracted not only those in search of relaxation, but also those seeking inspiration. The clear air and soft light have particularly appealed to some of Western culture's most outstanding painters, such as <a href="/wiki/Marc_Chagall" title="Marc Chagall">Marc Chagall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Matisse" title="Henri Matisse">Henri Matisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niki_de_Saint_Phalle" title="Niki de Saint Phalle">Niki de Saint Phalle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arman" title="Arman">Arman</a>. Their work is commemorated in many of the city's museums, including <i>Mus√©e Marc Chagall</i>, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Matisse_(Nice)" title="Mus√©e Matisse (Nice)">Mus√©e Matisse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_des_Beaux-Arts_de_Nice" title="Mus√©e des Beaux-Arts de Nice">Mus√©e des Beaux-Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Nice has the second largest hotel capacity in the country<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and it is one of its most visited cities, receiving 4&#160;million tourists every year.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> It also has the third busiest <a href="/wiki/Nice_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur_Airport" title="Nice C√¥te d'Azur Airport">airport</a> in France, after the two main Parisian ones.<sup id="cite_ref-aeroport_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aeroport-8">[8]</a></sup> It is the historical capital city of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Nice" title="County of Nice">County of Nice</a> (<i>Comt√© de Nice</i>).</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Nice" title="Timeline of Nice">Timeline of Nice</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_pre-Roman_Gaul" title="Greeks in pre-Roman Gaul">Greeks in pre-Roman Gaul</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg/220px-Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg/330px-Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg/440px-Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2620" data-file-height="2076" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maps-roman-empire-peak-150AD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nice in the time of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first known hominid settlements in the Nice area date back about 400,000 years;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> the <i><a href="/wiki/Terra_Amata_(archaeological_site)" title="Terra Amata (archaeological site)">Terra Amata</a></i> archeological site shows one of the earliest uses of fire, construction of houses, and flint findings dated to around 230,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Nice (Nicaea) was probably founded around 350 BC by the Greeks of Massalia (<a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>), and was given the name of <i>Nikaia</i> (ŒùŒØŒ∫Œ±ŒπŒ±) in honour of a victory over the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Ligures" title="Ligures">Ligurians</a>; <a href="/wiki/Nike_(mythology)" title="Nike (mythology)">Nike</a> (ŒùŒØŒ∫Œ∑) was the <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek goddess</a> of victory. The city soon became one of the busiest trading ports on the Ligurian coast; but it had an important rival in the Roman town of <a href="/wiki/Cemenelum" class="mw-redirect" title="Cemenelum">Cemenelum</a>, which continued to exist as a separate city until the time of the <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombard</a> invasions. The ruins of Cemenelum are in <a href="/wiki/Cimiez" title="Cimiez">Cimiez</a>, now a district of Nice.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_development">Early development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Nice" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Nice">Roman Catholic Diocese of Nice</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg/170px-Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg/255px-Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg/340px-Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2673" data-file-height="4024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_tour_Saint-Francois.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Tower of St Fran√ßois</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 7th century, Nice joined the <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a> League formed by the towns of <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a>. In 729 the city repulsed the <a href="/wiki/Saracens" class="mw-redirect" title="Saracens">Saracens</a>; but in 859 and again in 880 the Saracens pillaged and burned it, and for most of the 10th century remained masters of the surrounding country.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Nice participated in the wars and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Italy" title="History of Italy">history of Italy</a>. As an ally of <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">Pisa</a> it was the enemy of <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, and both the <a href="/wiki/King_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="King of France">King of France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Emperor</a> endeavoured to subjugate it; but in spite of this it maintained its municipal liberties. During the 13th and 14th centuries the city fell more than once into the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Counts_of_Provence" class="mw-redirect" title="Counts of Provence">Counts of Provence</a>, but it regained its independence even though related to Genoa.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Italia_1494-es.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Italia_1494-es.svg/170px-Italia_1494-es.svg.png" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Italia_1494-es.svg/255px-Italia_1494-es.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Italia_1494-es.svg/340px-Italia_1494-es.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3481" data-file-height="4167" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Italia_1494-es.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Duchy of Savoy (red) and other independent Italian states in 1494.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defences">Defences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Defences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The medieval city walls surrounded the Old Town. The landward side was protected by the River <a href="/wiki/Paillon" title="Paillon">Paillon</a>, which was later covered over and is now the tram route towards the Acropolis.</p>
<p>The east side of the town was protected by fortifications on <a href="/wiki/Castle_of_Nice#Castle_Hill" title="Castle of Nice">Castle Hill</a>. Another river flowed into the port on the east side of Castle Hill. Engravings suggest that the port area was also defended by walls.</p>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Monoprix" title="Monoprix">Monoprix</a> in Place de Garibaldi are excavated remains of a well-defended city gate on the main road from <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nice_and_Savoy">Nice and Savoy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nice and Savoy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Savoy" title="Duchy of Savoy">Duchy of Savoy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plan-Nice-1624.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Plan-Nice-1624.jpg/220px-Plan-Nice-1624.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Plan-Nice-1624.jpg/330px-Plan-Nice-1624.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Plan-Nice-1624.jpg/440px-Plan-Nice-1624.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1974" data-file-height="1530" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plan-Nice-1624.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nice in 1624</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Italia_1843.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Italia_1843.svg/170px-Italia_1843.svg.png" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Italia_1843.svg/255px-Italia_1843.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Italia_1843.svg/340px-Italia_1843.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="4200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Italia_1843.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kingdom of Piedmont-Sardinia (blue) and other independent Italian states in 1843.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1388 the commune placed itself under the protection of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Savoy" title="County of Savoy">Counts of Savoy</a>. Nice participated ‚Äì directly or indirectly ‚Äì in the history of <a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">Savoy</a> until 1860.</p>
<p>The maritime strength of Nice now rapidly increased until it was able to cope with the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a>; the fortifications were largely extended and the roads to the city improved. In 1561 <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Philibert,_Duke_of_Savoy" title="Emmanuel Philibert, Duke of Savoy">Emmanuel Philibert, Duke of Savoy</a> abolished the use of Latin as an administrative language and established the <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian language</a> as the official language of government affairs in Nice.</p>
<p>During the struggle between <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> great damage was caused by the passage of the armies invading <a href="/wiki/Provence" title="Provence">Provence</a>; <a href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Infectious disease">pestilence</a> and famine raged in the city for several years. In 1538, in the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Villeneuve-Loubet" title="Villeneuve-Loubet">Villeneuve-Loubet</a>, through the mediation of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_III" title="Pope Paul III">Pope Paul III</a>, the two monarchs concluded a <a href="/wiki/Truce_of_Nice" class="mw-redirect" title="Truce of Nice">ten years' truce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1543, Nice was attacked by the united <a href="/wiki/Franco-Ottoman_alliance" title="Franco-Ottoman alliance">Franco-Ottoman forces</a> of Francis I and <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Barbarossa Hayreddin Pasha</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Nice" title="Siege of Nice">Siege of Nice</a>; though the inhabitants repulsed the assault which followed the terrible bombardment, they were ultimately compelled to surrender, and Barbarossa was allowed to pillage the city and to carry off 2,500 captives. Pestilence appeared again in 1550 and 1580.</p>
<p>In 1600, Nice was briefly taken by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Guise" title="House of Guise">Duke of Guise</a>. By opening the ports of the county to all nations, and proclaiming full freedom of trade (1626), the commerce of the city was given great stimulus, the noble families taking part in its mercantile enterprises.</p>
<p>Captured by <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Catinat" title="Nicolas Catinat">Nicolas Catinat</a> in 1691, Nice was restored to <a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">Savoy</a> in 1696; but <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Nice_(1705)" title="Siege of Nice (1705)">it was again besieged by the French in 1705</a>, and in the following year its <a href="/wiki/Citadel" title="Citadel">citadel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">ramparts</a> were demolished.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht_(1713)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht (1713)">Treaty of Utrecht (1713)</a> once more gave the city back to the Duke of Savoy, who was on that same occasion recognised as King of Sicily. In the peaceful years which followed, the "new town" was built. From 1744 until the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)</a> the French and Spaniards were again in possession. In 1775 the king, who in 1718 had swapped his sovereignty of Sicily for the Kingdom of Sardinia, destroyed all that remained of the ancient liberties of the <a href="/wiki/Commune_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Commune in France">commune</a>. Conquered in 1792 by the armies of the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="First French Republic">First French Republic</a>, the County of Nice continued to be part of France until 1814; but after that date it reverted to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Piedmont-Sardinia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Piedmont-Sardinia">Kingdom of Piedmont-Sardinia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Nice">French Nice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: French Nice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turin_(1860)" title="Treaty of Turin (1860)">Treaty of Turin</a> was signed in 1860 between the <a href="/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_II_of_Italy" title="Victor Emmanuel II of Italy">Sardinian king</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a>, the County was again and definitively ceded to France as a territorial reward for French assistance in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Italian_War_of_Independence" title="Second Italian War of Independence">Second Italian War of Independence</a> against <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, which saw <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a> united with <a href="/wiki/Piedmont-Sardinia" class="mw-redirect" title="Piedmont-Sardinia">Piedmont-Sardinia</a>. The cession was ratified by a regional <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>: over 25,000 electors out of a total of 30,700 were in favour of the attachment to <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. Savoy was also transferred to the French crown by similar means. <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a>, born in Nice, opposed the cession to France, arguing that the ballot was rigged by the French. <a href="/wiki/Italia_irredenta" class="mw-redirect" title="Italia irredenta">Italian irredentists</a> considered the acquisition of Nice to be one of their main nationalist goals, along with <a href="/wiki/Istria" title="Istria">Istria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trentino" title="Trentino">Trentino</a>. In 1942‚Äì1943 the city was occupied and administered by Italy.</p>
<p>The 20th century saw the arrival of modern transportation. In 1900, the <a href="/wiki/Tramway_de_Nice_et_du_Littoral" class="mw-redirect" title="Tramway de Nice et du Littoral">Tramway de Nice</a> electrified its horse-drawn streetcars and spread its network to the entire <i>d√©partement</i> from <a href="/wiki/Menton" title="Menton">Menton</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cagnes-sur-Mer" title="Cagnes-sur-Mer">Cagnes-sur-Mer</a>. By the 1930s more bus connections were added in the area. In the 1930s Nice hosted international car racing in the <a href="/wiki/Formula_Libre" title="Formula Libre">Formula Libre</a> (predecessor to <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a>) on the so-called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Circuit_Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Circuit Nice (page does not exist)">Circuit Nice</a>. The circuit started along the waterfront just south of the Jardin Albert I, then headed westward along the <a href="/wiki/Promenade_des_Anglais" title="Promenade des Anglais">Promenade des Anglais</a> followed by a hairpin turn at the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Negresco" title="Hotel Negresco">Hotel Negresco</a> to come back eastward and around the Jardin Albert I before heading again east along the beach on the Quai des Etats-Unis.</p>
<p>As war broke out in September 1939, Nice became a city of refuge for many displaced foreigners, notably Jews fleeing the Nazi progression into Eastern Europe. From Nice many sought further shelter in the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonies</a>, Morocco and North and South America. After July 1940 and the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy Regime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitic</a> aggressions accelerated the exodus, starting in July 1941 and continuing through 1942. On 26 August 1942, 655 Jews of foreign origin were rounded up by the Laval government and interned in the Auvare barracks. Of these, 560 were deported to <a href="/wiki/Drancy_internment_camp" title="Drancy internment camp">Drancy internment camp</a> on 31 August 1942. Due to the activity of the Jewish banker <a href="/wiki/Angelo_Donati" title="Angelo Donati">Angelo Donati</a> and of the Capuchin friar <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A8re_Marie-Beno%C3%AEt" title="P√®re Marie-Beno√Æt">P√®re Marie-Beno√Æt</a> the local authorities hindered the application of anti-Jewish Vichy laws.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/French_Resistance" title="French Resistance"><i>r√©sistants</i></a> to the new regime were a group of High School seniors of the Lyc√©e de Nice, now Lyc√©e Mass√©na, in September 1940, later arrested and executed in 1944 near <a href="/wiki/Verdon_Gorge" title="Verdon Gorge">Castellane</a>. The first public demonstrations occurred on 14 July 1942 when several hundred protesters took to the streets along the Avenue de la Victoire and in the Place Mass√©na. In November 1942 German troops moved into most of unoccupied France, but Italian troops moved into a smaller zone including Nice. A certain ambivalence remained among the population, many of whom were recent immigrants of Italian ancestry. However, the resistance gained momentum after the Italian surrender in 1943 when the German army occupied the former Italian zone. Reprisals intensified between December 1943 and July 1944, when many partisans were tortured and executed by the local <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Milice" title="Milice">French Milice</a>. Nice was also heavily bombarded by American aircraft in preparation for the Allied <a href="/wiki/Operation_Dragoon" title="Operation Dragoon">landing in Provence</a> (1000 dead or wounded and more than 5600 people homeless) and famine ensued during summer 1944. American paratroopers entered the city on 30 August 1944 and Nice was finally liberated. The consequences of the war were heavy: the population decreased by 15% and economic life was totally disrupted.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg/220px-Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg/330px-Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg/440px-Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colline_du_chateau_waterfall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The waterfall on the Colline du Ch√¢teau (Castle Hill)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the second half of the 20th century, Nice enjoyed an economic boom primarily driven by tourism and construction. Two men dominated this period: <a href="/wiki/Jean_M%C3%A9decin" title="Jean M√©decin">Jean M√©decin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayor_(France)" title="Mayor (France)">mayor</a> for 33 years from 1928 to 1943 and from 1947 to 1965, and his son <a href="/wiki/Jacques_M%C3%A9decin" title="Jacques M√©decin">Jacques</a>, mayor for 24 years from 1966 to 1990. Under their leadership, there was extensive urban renewal, including many new constructions. These included the convention centre, theatres, new thoroughfares and expressways. The arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pieds-Noirs</a>, refugees from Algeria after 1962 independence, also gave the city a boost and somewhat changed the make-up of its population and traditional views. By the late 1980s, rumors of political corruption in the city government surfaced; and eventually formal accusations against Jacques M√©decin forced him to flee France in 1990. Later arrested in <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> in 1993, he was extradited back to France in 1994, convicted of several counts of corruption and associated crimes and sentenced to imprisonment.</p>
<p>On 16 October 1979, a <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslide</a> and an undersea slide caused two <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunamis</a> that hit the western coast of Nice; these <a href="/wiki/1979_Nice_events" class="mw-redirect" title="1979 Nice events">events</a> killed between 8 and 23 people.</p>
<p>In February 2001, European leaders met in Nice to negotiate and sign what is now the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nice" title="Treaty of Nice">Treaty of Nice</a>, amending the institutions of the European Union.</p>
<p>In 2003, local Chief <a href="/wiki/Prosecutor" title="Prosecutor">Prosecutor</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ric_de_Montgolfier" title="√âric de Montgolfier">√âric de Montgolfier</a> alleged that some judicial cases involving local personalities had been suspiciously derailed by the local judiciary, which he suspected of having unhealthy contacts through <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">Masonic</a> lodges with the defendants. A controversial official report stated later that Montgolfier had made unwarranted accusations.</p>
<p>On 14 July 2016, a truck was <a href="/wiki/2016_Nice_attack" title="2016 Nice attack">deliberately driven into a crowd of people</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Lahouaiej-Bouhlel" title="Mohamed Lahouaiej-Bouhlel">Mohamed Lahouaiej-Bouhlel</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Promenade_des_Anglais" title="Promenade des Anglais">Promenade des Anglais</a>. The crowd was watching a fireworks display in celebration of <a href="/wiki/Bastille_Day" title="Bastille Day">Bastille Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Eighty-seven people were killed, including the perpetrator, who was shot dead by police.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Another 202 were injured, with 52 in critical care and 25 in intensive care, according to the Paris prosecutor.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_Arms.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Nice_Arms.svg/170px-Nice_Arms.svg.png" width="170" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Nice_Arms.svg/255px-Nice_Arms.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Nice_Arms.svg/340px-Nice_Arms.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="660" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_Arms.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Arms of the County of Nice</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of Nice appeared for the first time in a copy of the <i>Regulations</i> of <a href="/wiki/Amadeus_VIII_of_Savoy" class="mw-redirect" title="Amadeus VIII of Savoy">Amadeus VIII</a>, probably written around 1430.<sup id="cite_ref-schor_22_23_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schor_22_23-17">[17]</a></sup> The Nice is symbolised by a red eagle on white background, placed on three mountains, which can be described in French <a href="/wiki/Heraldic" class="mw-redirect" title="Heraldic">heraldic</a> language as "d'argent √† une aigle de gueule pos√©e sur trois coupeaux".<sup id="cite_ref-schor_22_23_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schor_22_23-17">[17]</a></sup> ("Upon argent a red eagle is displayed, posed upon three mounds.") The arms have only undergone minor changes: the eagle has become more and more stylised, it now "wears" a coronet for the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Nice" title="County of Nice">County of Nice</a>, and the three mountains are now surrounded by a stylised sea.<sup id="cite_ref-schor_22_23_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schor_22_23-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The presence of the eagle, an imperial emblem, shows that these arms are related to the power of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Savoy" title="House of Savoy">House of Savoy</a>. The eagle standing over the three hills is a depiction of Savoy, referring to its domination over the country around Nice.<sup id="cite_ref-schor_22_23_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schor_22_23-17">[17]</a></sup> The combination of white and red (argent and gules) is a reference to the colours of the <a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">flag of Savoy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-schor_22_23_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schor_22_23-17">[17]</a></sup> The three mountains symbolise a territorial honour, without concern for geographic realism.<sup id="cite_ref-schor_22_23_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schor_22_23-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg/170px-Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg/255px-Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg/340px-Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palais_de_justice_nice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Palais de Justice</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Located in the <a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-C√¥te d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-C√¥te d'Azur</a> <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_France" title="Regions of France">region</a>, Nice is a <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">commune</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_in_France" title="Prefectures in France">prefecture</a> (administrative capital) of the <a href="/wiki/Alpes-Maritimes" title="Alpes-Maritimes">Alpes-Maritimes</a> d√©partement. However, it is also the largest city in France that is not a regional capital; the much larger <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> is its regional capital. <a href="/wiki/Christian_Estrosi" title="Christian Estrosi">Christian Estrosi</a> was elected as mayor in 2008. He was reelected for a second term in April 2014 ( that will end in 2020). He is a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Republicans_(France)" title="The Republicans (France)">the Republicans</a> (formerly the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_a_Popular_Movement" title="Union for a Popular Movement">Union for a Popular Movement</a>), the party supporting former President <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a>. He resigned in June 2016. Philippe Pradal replaced him as mayor on 13 June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> On 16 May 2017, he became mayor again after resigning from his seat as president of the regional council.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is divided over 9 <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_France" title="Cantons of France">cantons</a>: <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-1" title="Canton of Nice-1">Nice-1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-2" title="Canton of Nice-2">2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-3" title="Canton of Nice-3">3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-4" title="Canton of Nice-4">4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-5" title="Canton of Nice-5">5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-6" title="Canton of Nice-6">6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-7" title="Canton of Nice-7">7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-8" title="Canton of Nice-8">8</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Nice-9" title="Canton of Nice-9">9</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nice has a <a href="/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot-summer Mediterranean climate">hot-summer Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K√∂ppen climate classification">K√∂ppen</a>: <i>Csa</i>), enjoying mild winters with moderate rainfall. It is one of the warmest Mediterranean climates for its latitude. Summers are warm to hot, dry, and sunny. Rainfall is rare in this season, and a typical July month only records one or two days with measurable rainfall. The temperature is typically above 20&#160;¬∞C (68&#160;¬∞F) and frequently reaches 30&#160;¬∞C (86&#160;¬∞F). The climate data is recorded from the airport, located just metres from the sea. Summer temperatures, therefore, are often higher in the city. The average maximum temperature in the warmest months of July and August is about 27&#160;¬∞C (81&#160;¬∞F). The highest recorded temperature was 37.7&#160;¬∞C (99.9&#160;¬∞F) on 1 August 2006. Autumn generally starts sunny in September and becomes more cloudy and rainy towards October, while temperatures usually remain above 20&#160;¬∞C (68&#160;¬∞F) until November where days start to cool down to around 17&#160;¬∞C (63&#160;¬∞F). Winters are characterised by mild days (11 to 17&#160;¬∞C (52 to 63&#160;¬∞F)), cool nights (4 to 9&#160;¬∞C (39 to 48&#160;¬∞F)), and variable weather. Days can be either sunny and dry or damp and rainy. Frost is unusual and snowfalls are so extremely rare that they are remembered by inhabitants as special events. The average minimum temperature in January is around 5&#160;¬∞C (41&#160;¬∞F). Spring starts mild and rainy in late March, and is increasingly warm and sunny towards June.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vegetation_and_geography">Vegetation and geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Vegetation and geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The natural vegetation of Nice is typical for a Mediterranean landscape, with a heavy representation of broadleaf evergreen shrubs. Trees tend to be scattered but form dense forests in some areas. Large native tree species include evergreens such as <a href="/wiki/Quercus_ilex" title="Quercus ilex">holm oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stone_pine" title="Stone pine">stone pine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arbutus" title="Arbutus">arbutus</a>. Many introduced species grow in parks and gardens. <a href="/wiki/Palm_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Palm tree">Palms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citrus_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus fruit">citrus fruits</a> are among the trees which give Nice a subtropical appearance. But there are also species familiar to temperate areas around the world; examples include <a href="/wiki/Horse-chestnut_(tree)" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse-chestnut (tree)">horse chestnut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tilia" title="Tilia">linden</a> and even <a href="/wiki/Norway_spruce" class="mw-redirect" title="Norway spruce">Norway spruce</a>.</p>
<p>Geographically, Nice consists of two large bays. <a href="/wiki/Villefranche-sur-Mer" title="Villefranche-sur-Mer">Villefranche-sur-Mer</a> sits on an enclosed bay, while the main expanse of the city lies between the old port city and the Aeroport de C√¥te d'Azur, across a gently curving bay. The city rises from the flat beach into gentle rising hills, then is bounded by surrounding mountains that represent the Southern and nearly the Western extent of the <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_Alps" title="Ligurian Alps">Ligurian Alps</a> range.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_tourism">Economy and tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy and tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NiceVieuxCartier.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/NiceVieuxCartier.JPG/220px-NiceVieuxCartier.JPG" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/NiceVieuxCartier.JPG/330px-NiceVieuxCartier.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/NiceVieuxCartier.JPG/440px-NiceVieuxCartier.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="1228" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NiceVieuxCartier.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the old town</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nice is the seat of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chambre_de_commerce_et_d%27industrie_Nice_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chambre de commerce et d'industrie Nice C√¥te d'Azur (page does not exist)">Chambre de commerce et d'industrie Nice C√¥te d'Azur</a>. It manages the <a href="/wiki/Nice_-_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Nice - C√¥te d'Azur Airport">Nice - C√¥te d'Azur Airport</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_-_Mandelieu_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannes - Mandelieu Airport">Cannes - Mandelieu Airport</a>, as well as the Port of Nice. Investors from France and abroad can benefit from the assistance of the C√¥te d'Azur Economic Development Agency <a href="/w/index.php?title=Team_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Team C√¥te d'Azur (page does not exist)">Team C√¥te d'Azur</a>.</p>
<p>Among tourists, Nice is the second most popular French city after Paris<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, a fact which, combined with the difficulties of land travel at long distance (partly because of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>), allows it to have the third busiest airport in France in terms of passenger numbers (close to 10,000,000 passengers in 2005). It is easily accessible, being less than 6 hours from Paris by train, and the airport is located just minutes away from the city.</p>
<p>Nice has one conference centre: the <a href="/wiki/Palais_des_Congr%C3%A8s_Acropolis" title="Palais des Congr√®s Acropolis">Palais des Congr√®s Acropolis</a>. The city also has several business parks, including <a href="/w/index.php?title=Districts_of_businesses_Ni%C3%A7oise_L%27_Arenas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Districts of businesses Ni√ßoise L' Arenas (page does not exist)">l'Arenas</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Districts_of_Ni%C3%A7oise_Nice_businesses_Plaine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Districts of Ni√ßoise Nice businesses Plaine (page does not exist)">Nice the Plain</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Districts_of_businesses_Ni%C3%A7oise_Nice_M%C3%A9ridia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Districts of businesses Ni√ßoise Nice M√©ridia (page does not exist)">Nice M√©ridia</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Districts_of_businesses_Ni%C3%A7oise_Saint_Isidore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Districts of businesses Ni√ßoise Saint Isidore (page does not exist)">Saint Isidore</a>, and the Northern Forum.</p>
<p>In addition, the city features several shopping centres such as Nicetoile, Nice TNL, Nice Lingosti√®re, Northern Forum, St-Isidore, the Trinity (around the <a href="/wiki/Auchan" title="Auchan">Auchan</a> <a href="/wiki/Hypermarket" title="Hypermarket">hypermarket</a>) and Cap3000 in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Laurent-du-Var" title="Saint-Laurent-du-Var">Saint-Laurent-du-Var</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sophia_Antipolis" title="Sophia Antipolis">Sophia Antipolis</a> is a technology park northwest of <a href="/wiki/Antibes" title="Antibes">Antibes</a>. Much of the park is within the commune of <a href="/wiki/Valbonne" title="Valbonne">Valbonne</a>. Established between 1970 and 1984, it primarily houses companies in the fields of computing, electronics, pharmacology and biotechnology. Several institutions of higher learning are also located here, along with the European headquarters of W3C. The park is named after Sophie Glikman-Toumarkine, the wife of French Senator Pierre Laffitte, founder of the park, and incidentally, Sophia, the goddess of wisdom. The second half of the park's name is derived from Antipolis, the ancient Greek name of Antibes.</p>
<p>The Nice metropolitan area had a <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">GDP amounting to $47.7 billion</a>, and $34,480 per capita,<sup id="cite_ref-Brookings_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brookings-23">[23]</a></sup> slightly lower than the French average.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>Port</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_port.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Nice_port.jpg/220px-Nice_port.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Nice_port.jpg/330px-Nice_port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Nice_port.jpg/440px-Nice_port.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4203" data-file-height="2790" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_port.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The port of Nice</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The port of Nice is also known as Lympia port. This name comes from the Lympia spring which fed a small lake in a marshy zone where work on the port was started in 1745. Today this is the principal harbour installation of Nice ‚Äì there is also a small port in the Carras district. The port is the first port cement manufacturer in France, linked to the treatment plants of the rollers of the valley of Paillon. Fishing activities remain but the number of professional fishermen is now less than 10. Nice, being the point of continental France nearest to <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>, has ferry connections with the island developed with the arrival of NGV (<i>navires √† grande vitesse</i>) or <a href="/wiki/High-speed_craft" title="High-speed craft">high-speed craft</a>. Two companies provide the connections: <a href="/wiki/SNCM" class="mw-redirect" title="SNCM">SNCM</a>, a partially public company and <a href="/wiki/Corsica_Ferries" class="mw-redirect" title="Corsica Ferries">Corsica Ferries</a> ‚Äì Sardinia Ferries, an entirely private company. Located in front of the port, the Place Cassini has been renamed Place of Corsica.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Nice C√¥te d'Azur Airport</dt>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nice_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur_Airport" title="Nice C√¥te d'Azur Airport">Nice C√¥te d'Azur Airport</a> is the third most important airport in France after <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Charles de Gaulle Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orly_Airport" title="Orly Airport">Orly Airport</a>, both in Paris. It is on the <a href="/wiki/Promenade_des_Anglais" title="Promenade des Anglais">Promenade des Anglais</a>, near l'Ar√©nas and has two <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminals</a>. Due to its proximity to the Principality of <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, it also serves as that city‚Äìstate's airport. A helicopter service provided by <a href="/wiki/Heli_Air_Monaco" title="Heli Air Monaco">Heli Air Monaco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monacair" title="Monacair">Monacair</a> links the city and airport; it averages 39 flights a day. It is run by the Chamber of Commerce and the Nice C√¥te d'Azur industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2009)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Its director is Herv√© de Place, director of the C√¥te d'Azur airports, which includes <a href="/wiki/Cannes_-_Mandelieu_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannes - Mandelieu Airport">Cannes - Mandelieu Airport</a>. In 2009, 9,830,987 passengers travelled through the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-traffic_details_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-traffic_details-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Rail</dt>
</dl>
<p>The main railway station is <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Nice-Ville" title="Gare de Nice-Ville">Nice-Ville</a>, served both by high speed <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> trains connecting Paris and Nice in less than 6 hours and by local commuter <a href="/wiki/TER_Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te-d%27Azur" title="TER Provence-Alpes-C√¥te-d'Azur">TER</a> services. <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Marseille-Saint-Charles" title="Gare de Marseille-Saint-Charles">Marseille</a> is reached in 2.5 hours. Nice also has international connections to Italy, Switzerland, Belgium, and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Nice is also served by several suburban stations including Nice St-Augustin, Nice St-Roch and Nice Riquier.</p>
<p>Nice is also the southern terminus of the independently run <a href="/wiki/Chemins_de_Fer_de_Provence" title="Chemins de Fer de Provence">Chemins de Fer de Provence</a> railway line which connects the city with <a href="/wiki/Digne" class="mw-redirect" title="Digne">Digne</a> in approximatively 4 hours. A metro-like suburban service is also provided on the southern part of the line.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Tram</dt>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tramway_de_Nice_et_du_Littoral" class="mw-redirect" title="Tramway de Nice et du Littoral">Tramway de Nice</a> began operating horse-drawn trams in 1879. Electrified in 1900, the combined length of the network reached 144&#160;km (89.48&#160;mi) by 1930. The replacement of trams with <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybuses</a> began in 1948 and was completed in 1953. In 2007, the new <a href="/wiki/Nice_tramway" title="Nice tramway">Tramway de Nice</a> linked the northern and eastern suburbs via the city centre. Two other lines are currently in the planning stage. The second line will run east-west from Place Mass√©na to the <a href="/wiki/Nice_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur_Airport" title="Nice C√¥te d'Azur Airport">Nice C√¥te d'Azur Airport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> extending to <a href="/wiki/Cagnes-sur-Mer" title="Cagnes-sur-Mer">Cagnes-sur-Mer</a> and Le Port, while the third line will provide a connection to the future TGV Nice Saint-Augustin Lingosti√®re rail station.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Road</dt>
</dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/A8_autoroute" title="A8 autoroute">A8 autoroute</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Route_nationale_7" title="Route nationale 7">Route nationale 7</a> pass through the Nice agglomeration, linking Marseille with Italy.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sights">Sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice-seafront.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Nice-seafront.jpg/220px-Nice-seafront.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Nice-seafront.jpg/330px-Nice-seafront.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Nice-seafront.jpg/440px-Nice-seafront.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice-seafront.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Promenade_des_Anglais" title="Promenade des Anglais">Promenade des Anglais</a> ("Promenade of the English") is a promenade along the Baie des Anges ("Bay of the Angels"), which is a bay of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>, in Nice. Before Nice was urbanised, the coastline at Nice was just bordered by a deserted stretch of <a href="/wiki/Shingle_beach" title="Shingle beach">shingle beach</a> (covered with large pebbles). The first houses were located on higher ground well away from the sea, as wealthy tourists visiting Nice in the 18th century did not come for the beach, but for the gentle winter weather. The areas close to the water were home to Nice's dockworkers and fishermen.</p>
<p>In the second half of the 18th century, many wealthy English people took to spending the winter in Nice, enjoying the panorama along the coast. When a particularly harsh winter up north brought an influx of beggars to Nice, some of the rich Englishmen proposed a useful project for them: the construction of a walkway (<i>chemin de promenade</i>) along the sea.</p>
<p>The city of Nice, intrigued by the prospect of a pleasant promenade, greatly increased the scope of the work. The Promenade was first called the <i>Camin dei Angl√®s</i> (the English Way) by the Ni√ßois in their native dialect, <a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%A7ard" class="mw-redirect" title="Ni√ßard">Nissart</a>. After the annexation of Nice by France in 1860 it was rechristened <i>La Promenade des Anglais</i>, replacing the former Nissart name with its French translation.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Negresco" title="Hotel Negresco">Hotel Negresco</a> on the Promenade des Anglais was named after <a href="/wiki/Henri_Negresco" title="Henri Negresco">Henri Negresco</a> (1868‚Äì1920) who had the palatial hotel constructed in 1912. In keeping with the conventions of the time, when the Negresco first opened in 1913 its front opened on the side opposite the Mediterranean.</p>
<p>Another place worth mentioning is the small street parallel to the Promenade des Anglais, leading from Nice's downtown, beginning at Place Mass√©na and running parallel to the promenade in the direction of the airport for a short distance of about 4 blocks. This section of the city is referred to as the "Zone Pietonne", or "Pedestrian Zone". Cars are not allowed (with exception to delivery trucks), making this avenue a popular walkway. Here, tourists can find a fine selection of restaurants, specializing in various types of cuisine, including Ni√ßoise, French, Japanese, Chinese, Vietnamese, Spanish and Italian. There is also a large selection of caf√©s where one can sit and enjoy an ap√©ritif, as well as several bakeries with coffee, cake, and a terrace. There are also plenty of small shops selling clothing, shoes, and souvenirs.</p>
<p>Old Nice is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ra_de_Nice" title="Op√©ra de Nice">Op√©ra de Nice</a>. It was constructed at the end of the 19th century under the design of Fran√ßois Aune, to replace King Charles F√©lix's Maccarani Theater. Today, it is open to the public and provides a regular program of performances.</p>
<p>Other sights include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Castle_of_Nice" title="Castle of Nice">Ch√¢teau</a></li>
<li><i>Monument aux morts</i></li>
<li>The port</li>

<li><i><a href="/wiki/Jardin_botanique_de_la_Ville_de_Nice" title="Jardin botanique de la Ville de Nice">Jardin botanique de la Ville de Nice</a></i> (botanical garden)</li>
<li><i>Musee Massena</i></li>
<li><i>March√© aux fleurs</i></li>
<li>Old Nice</li>
<li><i>Grand H√¥tel Imp√©rial</i></li>
<li>Fort of Mont Alban</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Squares">Squares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Squares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Place_Mass√©na"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Place_Mass.C3.A9na">Place Mass√©na</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Place Mass√©na">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Placemassena1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Placemassena1.JPG/220px-Placemassena1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Placemassena1.JPG/330px-Placemassena1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Placemassena1.JPG/440px-Placemassena1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>

<div class="thumb tright">

<p>The <i>Place Mass√©na</i> is the main square of the city. Before the <a href="/wiki/Paillon" title="Paillon">Paillon</a> River was covered over, the Pont-Neuf was the only practicable way between the old town and the modern one. The square was thus divided into two parts (North and South) in 1824. With the demolition of the Mass√©na Casino in 1979, the Place Mass√©na became more spacious and less dense and is now bordered by red ochre buildings of <a href="/wiki/Italian_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian architecture">Italian architecture</a>.</p>
<p>The recent rebuilding of the tramline gave the square back to the pedestrians, restoring its status as a real Mediterranean square. It is lined with palm trees and stone pines, instead of being the rectangular roundabout of sorts it had become over the years. Since its construction, the Place Mass√©na has always been the spot for great public events. It is used for concerts, and particularly during the summer festivals, the <i><a href="/wiki/Nice_Carnival" title="Nice Carnival">Corso carnavalesque</a></i> (carnival parade) in February, the military procession of 14 July (Bastille Day) or other traditional celebrations and banquets.</p>
<p>The Place Mass√©na is a two-minute walk from the <a href="/wiki/Promenade_des_Anglais" title="Promenade des Anglais">Promenade des Anglais</a>, old town, town centre, and Albert I Garden (<i>Jardin Albert Ier</i>). It is also a large crossroads between several of the main streets of the city: <i>avenue Jean M√©decin</i>, <i>avenue F√©lix Faure</i>, <i>boulevard Jean Jaur√®s</i>, <i>avenue de Verdun</i> and <i>rue Gioffredo</i>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Place_Garibaldi">Place Garibaldi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Place Garibaldi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg/170px-Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg" width="170" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg/255px-Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg/340px-Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2760" data-file-height="4506" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_Place_Garibaldi_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Garibaldi's monument, Place Garibaldi</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Place Garibaldi</i> also stands out for its architecture and history. It is named after <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a>, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a> (born in Nice in 1807 when Nice was part of the Napoleonic Empire, before reverting to the Kingdom of Piedmont-Sardinia). The square was built at the end of the 18th century and served as the entry gate to the city and end of the road to Turin. It took several names between 1780 and 1870 (Pla√ßa Pairouli√®ra, Place de la R√©publique, Place Napol√©on, Place d'Armes, Place Saint-Augustin, Piazza Vittorio) and finally Place Garibaldi in September 1870.</p>
<p>A statue of Garibaldi, who was fiercely in favour of the union of Nice with Italy, stands in the centre of the square. The recent rebuilding of the area to accommodate the new tramway line gave mostly the entire square to pedestrians. The architecture is in line with the Turin model, which was the norm of urban renewal throughout the entire realm of the House of Savoy.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg/220px-Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg/330px-Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg/440px-Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4097" data-file-height="2421" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_tramway_place_Garibaldi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Place Garibaldi, pedestrian since the introduction of the Nice tramway.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It is a crossroads between the <i>Vieux Nice</i> (old town) and the town centre. Place Garibaldi is close to the eastern districts of Nice, <i>Port Lympia</i> (Lympia Harbour), and the TNL commercial centre. This square is also a junction of several important streets: the <i>boulevard Jean-Jaur√®s</i>, the <i>avenue de la R√©publique</i>, the <i>rue Cassini</i> and the <i>rue Catherine-S√©gurane</i>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Place_Rossetti">Place Rossetti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Place Rossetti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg/220px-Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg/330px-Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg/440px-Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cath%C3%A9drale_Sainte_R%C3%A9parate_in_Nice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Cathedral</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Entirely enclosed and pedestrianised, this square is located in the heart of the old town. With typical buildings in red and yellow ochres surrounding the square, the <i>cath√©drale Sainte-R√©parate</i> and the fountain in the centre, <i>place Rossetti</i> is a must-see spot in the old town. By day, the place is invaded by the terraces of traditional restaurants and the finest ice-cream makers. By night, the environment changes radically, with tourists and youths flocking to the square, where music reverberates on the walls of the small square. The square's lighting at night gives it a magical aspect.</p>
<p>Place Rossetti is in the centre of the old town, streets <i>Jesus</i>, <i>Rossetti</i>, <i>Masco√Ønat</i> and the <i>Pont-vieux</i> (old bridge)</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cours_Saleya">Cours Saleya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cours Saleya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Saleya_nice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Saleya_nice.jpg/220px-Saleya_nice.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Saleya_nice.jpg/330px-Saleya_nice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Saleya_nice.jpg/440px-Saleya_nice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Saleya_nice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Saleya Course (2007)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Cours Saleya is situated parallel to the <i>Quai des √âtats-Unis</i>. In the past, it belonged to the upper classes. It is probably the most traditional square of the town, with its daily flower market. The <i>Cours Saleya</i> also opens on the <i>Palais des Rois Sardes</i> (Palace of the Kings of Sardinia). In the present, the <i>court</i> is mostly a place of entertainment.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Place_du_Palais">Place du Palais</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Place du Palais">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg/220px-NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg/330px-NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg/440px-NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="594" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NIKAIA-palaisN5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Place du Palais view of the Rusca palace</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As its name indicates, the <i>Place du Palais</i> is where the <i>Palais de la Justice</i> (Law courts) of Nice is located. On this square, there also is the <i>Palais Rusca</i>, which also belongs to the justice department (home of the <i>tribunal de grande instance</i>).</p>
<p>The square is also notable due to the presence of the city clock. Today, the <i>Place du Palais</i> is alive day and night. Often, groups of youths will hangout on the steps leading to the <i>Palais de la Justice</i>. Concerts, films, and other major public events frequently occur in this space.</p>
<p>It is situated halfway between the <i>Cours Saleya</i> and <i>Place Mass√©na</i>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>The city's major <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club is <a href="/wiki/OGC_Nice" title="OGC Nice">OGC Nice</a>. They play in <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a> (the top division in France).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Nice" title="Olympic Nice">Olympic Nice</a> swimming club (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><i>Olympic Nice Natation</i></span>) is also notable; <a href="/wiki/Camille_Muffat" title="Camille Muffat">Camille Muffat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yannick_Agnel" title="Yannick Agnel">Yannick Agnel</a> used to train there for example.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>Nice hosts the finish of the annual <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_road_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicycle road racing">cycling race</a> <a href="/wiki/Paris%E2%80%93Nice" title="Paris‚ÄìNice">Paris‚ÄìNice</a>.</li>
<li>The Nice hockey C√¥te d'Azur Club play in <a href="/wiki/Ligue_Magnus" title="Ligue Magnus">Ligue Magnus</a>, the top men's division of the French ice hockey pyramid.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Stade_Ni%C3%A7ois" title="Stade Ni√ßois">Stade Ni√ßois</a> is an amateur rugby club playing in <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_2" title="F√©d√©rale 2">F√©d√©rale 2</a>.</li>
</ul>
