<p>Sources&#160;: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://cassini.ehess.fr/cassini/fr/html/fiche.php?select_resultat=24984">Ldh/EHESS/Cassini until 1962</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.statistiques-locales.insee.fr/FICHES/DL/DEP/06/COM/DL_COM06088.pdf">INSEE database from 1968</a> (<a href="/wiki/Population_without_double_counting" title="Population without double counting">population without double counting</a> and municipal population from 2006)</p>
</center>
<p>The metropolitan area of Nice, defined by INSEE, is home to 888,784 inhabitants (fifth most populous in France) and its urban area totals 933,080 inhabitants, which makes it the sixth largest in France.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG/220px-Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG/330px-Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG/440px-Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3328" data-file-height="2146" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nice_vietnamese_restaurant_3630.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nice residents of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnamese</a> descent stand in front of one of the many Vietnamese restaurants of the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Roughly 10% of the population has foreign citizenship.</p>
<p>The six largest immigrant groups are from:</p>
<ol>
<li>Tunisia</li>
<li>Italy</li>
<li>Morocco</li>
<li>Algeria</li>
<li>Portugal</li>
<li>Spain<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ol>
<p>The city saw a big demographic rise in the second half of the 19th century, a period when the population more than doubled, mainly due to French immigration. At the beginning of the 20th century, this rise intensified with the arrival of internal immigrants from the County of Nice itself.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>After the First World War, the city had a strong increase in population. Immigration was again the reason of this growth. The hotel industry and that of the construction industry, in full strength in the 1920s, attracted the world more and more and thus made it possible for Nice to become a town of national importance. In 1921, Nice then became the eleventh most populous town of France, then in 1931, the eighth, before being ranked sixth in 1946; thereafter the city reached its current demographic level due to the arrival of sixty thousand people including French citizens from <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Since the 1970s, the number of inhabitants has not changed significantly; the relatively high migration to Nice is compensated by a natural negative growth of the population. Nice has a high proportion of elderly people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, and as such has one of the highest median ages in France.</p>
<p>Currently, the population of the city is growing again, the most likely reason of which is a preference for the climate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Nice was projected to have 360,000 citizens in 2008, and will have 370,000 by 2012.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Observatory">Observatory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Observatory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg/220px-Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg/330px-Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg/440px-Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="991" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coupole_Bischoffsheim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the Bischoffsheim cupola, main cupola of <a href="/wiki/Nice_Observatory" title="Nice Observatory">Nice Observatory</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Observatoire de Nice</i> (<a href="/wiki/Nice_Observatory" title="Nice Observatory">Nice Observatory</a>) is located on the summit of Mont Gros. The observatory was established in 1879 by the banker <a href="/wiki/Rapha%C3%ABl_Bischoffsheim" title="Rapha√´l Bischoffsheim">Rapha√´l Bischoffsheim</a>. The architect was <a href="/wiki/Charles_Garnier_(architect)" title="Charles Garnier (architect)">Charles Garnier</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Eiffel" title="Gustave Eiffel">Gustave Eiffel</a> designed the main dome.</p>
<p>The 76-cm (30-inch) <a href="/wiki/Refractor_telescope" class="mw-redirect" title="Refractor telescope">refractor telescope</a> that became operational in 1888 was at that time the world's largest telescope. It was outperformed one year later by the 36-inch (91-cm) refractor at the <a href="/wiki/Lick_Observatory" title="Lick Observatory">Lick Observatory</a> at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Cruz" title="University of California, Santa Cruz">University of California, Santa Cruz</a>.</p>
<p>As a scientific institution, the Nice Observatory was merged with <a href="/wiki/Centre_de_recherches_en_g%C3%A9odynamique_et_astrom%C3%A9trie" title="Centre de recherches en g√©odynamique et astrom√©trie">CERGA</a> in 1988 to form the <a href="/wiki/Observatoire_de_la_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" class="mw-redirect" title="Observatoire de la C√¥te d'Azur">Observatoire de la C√¥te d'Azur</a>. Many scientific activities still take place on the Nice Observatory site on Mount Gross above the city including gravity-wave and high-energy astrophysics, astrometric and interferometric astronomy and planetary science. The city is the namesake for the <a href="/wiki/Nice_model" title="Nice model">Nice model</a>, which was developed at the observatory in 2005.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nice is one of the oldest human settlements in the world. Terra-Amata, an archaeological site dating from the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Palaeolithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower Palaeolithic">Lower Palaeolithic</a> age, is situated near Nice. Nice itself was established by the ancient <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>. There was also an independent <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> city, Cemenelum, near Nice, where the hill of Cimiez is located. It is an archaeological site with treasures, of which only a small part has been excavated. The excavated site includes thermal baths, arenas and Roman road.</p>
<p>Since the 2nd century AD, the light of the city has attracted many famous painters and sculptors such as <a href="/wiki/Chagall" class="mw-redirect" title="Chagall">Chagall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matisse" class="mw-redirect" title="Matisse">Matisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niki_de_Saint_Phalle" title="Niki de Saint Phalle">Niki de Saint Phalle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yves_Klein" title="Yves Klein">Klein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arman" title="Arman">Arman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sacha_Sosno" title="Sacha Sosno">Sosno</a>. Nice inspired many composers and intellectuals in different countries e.g. <a href="/wiki/Hector_Berlioz" title="Hector Berlioz">Berlioz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rossini" class="mw-redirect" title="Rossini">Rossini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche" title="Friedrich Nietzsche">Nietzsche</a> etc.</p>
<p>Nice also has numerous museums of all kinds: <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Marc_Chagall" title="Mus√©e Marc Chagall">Mus√©e Marc Chagall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Matisse_(Nice)" title="Mus√©e Matisse (Nice)">Mus√©e Matisse</a> (arenas of Cimiez containing Roman ruins), <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_des_Beaux-Arts_de_Nice" title="Mus√©e des Beaux-Arts de Nice">Mus√©e des Beaux-Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_international_d%27Art_na%C3%AFf_Anatole_Jakovsky" title="Mus√©e international d'Art na√Øf Anatole Jakovsky">Mus√©e international d'Art na√Øf Anatole Jakovsky</a>, Mus√©e Terra-Amata, Museum of Asian Art, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_d%27art_moderne_et_d%27art_contemporain" title="Mus√©e d'art moderne et d'art contemporain">Mus√©e d'art moderne et d'art contemporain</a> which devotes much space to the well-known <i>√âcole of Nice</i> ‚Äù), Museum of Natural History, Mus√©e Mass√©na, Naval Museum and <i>Galerie des Ponchettes</i>.</p>
<p>Being a vacation resort, Nice hosts many festivals throughout the year, such as the Carnaval de Nice and the Nice Jazz Festival.</p>
<p>Nice has a distinct culture due to its unique history. The local language <i><a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%A7ard" class="mw-redirect" title="Ni√ßard">Ni√ßard</a> (Nissart)</i> is an <a href="/wiki/Occitan" class="mw-redirect" title="Occitan">Occitan</a> dialect (but some Italian scholars argue that it is a <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_language_(Romance)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ligurian language (Romance)">Ligurian</a> dialect). It is still spoken by a substantial minority. Strong <a href="/wiki/Italian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian culture">Italian</a> and (to a lesser extent) <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsican</a> influences make it more intelligible to Italians than other extant Proven√ßal dialects.</p>
<p>In the past, Nice welcomed many immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (who continue to make up a large proportion of the population), as well as Spanish and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> immigrants. However, in the past few decades immigration has been opened to include immigrants from all over the world, particularly those from former Northern and Western African colonies, as well as southeast Asia. Traditions are still alive, especially in <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> and dances. The most famous dance is the <a href="/wiki/Farandole" title="Farandole">farandole</a>.</p>
<p>Since 1860 a cannon (based at the Ch√¢teau east of Old Nice) is shot at twelve o'clock sharp. The detonation can be heard almost all over the city. This tradition goes back to Sir Thomas Coventry, who intended to remind the citizens of having lunch on time.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The cuisine of Nice is especially close to those of <a href="/wiki/Provence" title="Provence">Provence</a> but also <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">Piedmont</a> and uses local ingredients (<a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anchovies" class="mw-redirect" title="Anchovies">anchovies</a>, fruit and vegetables) but also those from more remote regions, in particular from Northern Europe, because ships which came to pick up olive oil arrived full of food products, such as dried <a href="/wiki/Haddock" title="Haddock">haddock</a>.</p>
<p>Nice has a few local dishes. There is a local tart made with onions and <a href="/wiki/Anchovies" class="mw-redirect" title="Anchovies">anchovies</a> (or anchovy paste), named "<a href="/wiki/Pissaladi%C3%A8re" title="Pissaladi√®re">Pissaladi√®re</a>". <i><a href="/wiki/Socca" class="mw-redirect" title="Socca">Socca</a></i> is a type of pancake made from <a href="/wiki/Chickpea" title="Chickpea">chickpea</a> flour. <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Farcis_ni%C3%A7ois&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Farcis ni√ßois (page does not exist)">Farcis ni√ßois</a></i> is a dish made from vegetables stuffed with a mixture of breadcrumbs, meat (generally sausage and ground beef), and herbs; and <i><a href="/wiki/Salade_ni%C3%A7oise" title="Salade ni√ßoise">salade ni√ßoise</a></i> is a tomato salad with green peppers of the "Corne" variety, baked eggs, tuna or anchovies, and olives.</p>
<p>Local meat comes from neighbouring valleys, such as the sheep of <a href="/wiki/Sisteron" title="Sisteron">Sisteron</a>. Local fish, such as mullets, bream, sea urchins, and anchovies (alevins) are used to a great extent, so much so that it has given birth to a proverb: "fish are born in the sea and die in oil".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Examples of Ni√ßois specialties include:</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beignets_de_fleurs_de_courgettes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Beignets de fleurs de courgettes (page does not exist)">Beignets de fleurs de courgettes</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ratatouille" title="Ratatouille">Ratatouille</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pichade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pichade (page does not exist)">Pichade</a></i></li>

<li><i><a href="/wiki/Socca" class="mw-redirect" title="Socca">Socca</a></i></li>

<h3><span id="Twin_towns_‚Äì_Sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_Sister_cities">Twin towns ‚Äì Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Twin towns ‚Äì Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
